## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). Nonlinear oscillators feature polynomial or transcendental restoring/damping forces beyond the linear harmonic case.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (nonlinear restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping depending on amplitude)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear restoring + driving)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force from pendulum dynamics)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity-dependent damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * v**3 (combined nonlinear terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope вҶ’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects вҶ’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay вҶ’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior вҶ’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects вҶ’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, xВі, xвҒө) вҶ’ symmetric potential well, preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power restoring forces (xВІ) вҶ’ asymmetric potential well, breaking oscillation symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to xВІВ·v вҶ’ amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol type self-excitation)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(cВ·t) or cos(cВ·t) вҶ’ external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Cubic position term xВі with same/opposite sign as linear term вҶ’ hardening/softening spring nonlinearity
- Odd powers of velocity (v, vВі) вҶ’ dissipative forces that depend on speed but reverse with direction
- Product of position and time-periodic function xВ·cos(cВ·t) вҶ’ parametric excitation / Mathieu-type instability
- Sinusoidal function of position sin(cВ·x) вҶ’ pendulum-like bounded restoring force with multiple equilibria

**x*|v|^(1/3):** This involves a fractional power of |v|. It cannot be represented by polynomials, exponentials, square roots of x, or trigonometric functions.
